			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2010–12 Algerian protests</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">

<p>The <b>2010–12 Algerian protests</b> were a continuing series of protests taking place throughout <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, which started on 28 December 2010. They have been inspired by similar <a href="/wiki/Arab_Spring" title="Arab Spring">protests across the Middle East and North Africa</a>. Causes cited by the protestors include <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, the lack of housing, food-price <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">corruption</a>, restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">freedom of speech</a> and poor <a href="/wiki/Living_conditions" class="mw-redirect" title="Living conditions">living conditions</a>. While localised protests were already commonplace over previous years, extending into December 2010, an unprecedented wave of simultaneous protests and riots, sparked by sudden rises in staple food prices, erupted all over the country starting in January 2011. These were quelled by government measures to lower food prices, but were followed by a wave of <a href="/wiki/Self-immolation" title="Self-immolation">self-immolations</a>, most of them in front of government buildings. Opposition parties, unions, and human rights organisations then began to hold weekly demonstrations, despite these being illegal without government permission under the ongoing <a href="/wiki/State_of_emergency" title="State of emergency">state of emergency</a>; the government suppressed these demonstrations as far as possible, but in late February yielded to pressure and lifted the state of emergency. Meanwhile, protests by unemployed youth, typically citing unemployment, <i>hogra</i> (oppression), and infrastructure problems, resumed, occurring almost daily in towns scattered all over the country.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After the riots of 1988, the Algerian government had moved towards democracy, holding free elections. However, when the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> (FIS) won the first free <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_1991" title="Algerian legislative election, 1991">parliamentary election</a> in 1991, the military staged a coup d'état, voided the election results, declared a state of emergency which remained in force until 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> and arrested the FIS leadership. This led to the founding of the <a href="/wiki/Armed_Islamic_Group_of_Algeria" title="Armed Islamic Group of Algeria">Armed Islamic Groups</a> (GIA) and the ten-year <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Civil_War" title="Algerian Civil War">Algerian Civil War</a>, in which an estimated 250,000 people were killed.</p>
<p>With the unchallenged <a href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_1999" title="Algerian presidential election, 1999">election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Abdelaziz_Bouteflika" title="Abdelaziz Bouteflika">Abdelaziz Bouteflika</a> as president in 1999, civilian government was nominally restored. Violence died down as both guerrillas and soldiers were given immunity for their previous acts under the controversial <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_Peace_and_National_Reconciliation" title="Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation">Charter for Peace and National Reconciliation</a>. Towards the end of his second term, Bouteflika amended the constitution to allow himself to run for a third term in 2009; to no one's surprise, he won the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Algerian_presidential_election,_2009" title="Algerian presidential election, 2009">election</a>, with, according to the opposition and the US Embassy, a very low turnout.</p>
<p>Seventy percent of Algeria's population is less than 30 years old. Consequent high levels of youth unemployment, coupled with corruption and widespread poverty, are seen as reasons for dissatisfaction.<sup id="cite_ref-afrik_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrik-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The leader of the <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Culture_and_Democracy" title="Rally for Culture and Democracy">Rally for Culture and Democracy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Sadi" title="Saïd Sadi">Saïd Sadi</a>, claimed that during 2010, there were "9,700 riots and unrests" in Algeria.<sup id="cite_ref-army_should_quit_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army_should_quit-5">[5]</a></sup> Some protests were about issues such as education and health care, as well as rampant corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Prior to the outbreak of protests, in February 2008, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> Ambassador <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stephen_Ford" title="Robert Stephen Ford">Robert Ford</a> in <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks_cables" class="mw-redirect" title="WikiLeaks cables">leaked</a> <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_cables" class="mw-redirect" title="Diplomatic cables">diplomatic cables</a> called Algeria "an unhappy country", stating "There is much discussion among political circles about the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Algeria" title="Constitution of Algeria">constitution</a>, the third term and the succession issue, but precious little discussion about how to address long-standing political alienation and social discontent throughout the country."<sup id="cite_ref-08ALGIERS198_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08ALGIERS198-7">[7]</a></sup> He claimed there were strikes over food "by <a href="/wiki/Trade_unions_in_Algeria" title="Trade unions in Algeria">different labor groups</a> almost weekly" and that "almost daily there are isolated demonstrations with the occasional government office in some distant town attacked."<sup id="cite_ref-08ALGIERS198_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08ALGIERS198-7">[7]</a></sup> Ford stated that "voter turnout for the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_2007" title="Algerian legislative election, 2007">2007 legislative</a> and local elections was lower than ever before because Algeria's young people do not see the political system as having any relevance to addressing their problem."<sup id="cite_ref-08ALGIERS198_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-08ALGIERS198-7">[7]</a></sup> United States diplomats also claimed that the Algerian regime is more corrupt than the international community realises and is also more fragile. The <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_cable" title="Diplomatic cable">diplomatic cable</a> also said that Bouteflika may have cancer.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="29_December_2010">29 December 2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 29 December 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 29 December 2010, clashes with police were reported in Algiers during protests about the lack of housing. At least 53 people were reported to have been injured and another 29 were arrested.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National.2C_3.E2.80.9310_January_2011">National, 3–10 January 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: National, 3–10 January 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2011, prices of basic foodstuffs rose significantly in Algeria,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> in line with global trends but also reflecting newly imposed regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2010-2011_Tunisian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2010-2011 Tunisian protests">Unprecedented protests in neighbouring Tunisia</a> over unemployment were already being reported, contributing to the mood.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Broken shop curtain with people looking inside." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg/170px-Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg/255px-Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg/340px-Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="432" data-file-height="576" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Renault-BEO-Incendi%C3%A9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Renault" title="Renault">Renault</a> shop of Triolet near Bab El Oued, burnt in the riots.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 3 and 10 January, riots and protests broke out across most Algerian towns, triggered by large increases in the prices of basic foods including oil, sugar, and flour. While localised riots have been a frequent occurrence in Algeria since 2005, this set of riots was the first to spread across most regions of the country simultaneously rather than being confined to a particular area. By 10 January they were limited to a few towns, but continued in those towns.<sup id="cite_ref-Beatrice_Khadige_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beatrice_Khadige-13">[13]</a></sup> More organised efforts to demonstrate on 11 January in Algiers were suppressed vigorously by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>Protests against the price increases started on 3 January, with protest in the Ras El Ain quarter of <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Voix_Oranie_PDF_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voix_Oranie_PDF-15">[15]</a></sup> and in <a href="/wiki/Fouka,_Algeria" title="Fouka, Algeria">Fouka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Staoueli" class="mw-redirect" title="Staoueli">Staoueli</a> near Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-Voix_Oranie_PDF_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voix_Oranie_PDF-15">[15]</a></sup> On 4 January they were repeated in Staoueli and spread to other areas near the capital, with impromptu roadblocks at Douaouda in <a href="/wiki/Tipasa" title="Tipasa">Tipasa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Voix_Oranie_PDF_15-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Voix_Oranie_PDF-15">[15]</a></sup> and Kolea<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 January, major riots broke out in several areas at once: in the Bab El Oued neighbourhood of the capital, <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> and nearby suburbs, as well as Algeria's second city, <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>, and other towns including <a href="/wiki/Djelfa" title="Djelfa">Djelfa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boumerdes" class="mw-redirect" title="Boumerdes">Boumerdes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tipaza" title="Tipaza">Tipaza</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The young men rioting blocked roads, burned tires, and sacked government buildings, protesting the sudden increase in the <a href="/wiki/Cost_of_living" title="Cost of living">cost of living</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> the demolition of <a href="/wiki/Shantytown" class="mw-redirect" title="Shantytown">shantytowns</a>, and broader issues such as unemployment.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> They were met by anti-riot forces, who attempted to disperse the crowds. In Bab El Oued, shops and car showrooms were also targeted.<sup id="cite_ref-watan1_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-watan1-21">[21]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Salvation_Front" title="Islamic Salvation Front">Islamic Salvation Front</a> number two <a href="/wiki/Ali_Belhadj" class="mw-redirect" title="Ali Belhadj">Ali Belhadj</a> went to Bab El Oued to see the events and encourage the youths; he was arrested later that day, as were many other protesters and rioters.<sup id="cite_ref-Djamel_Belayachi_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Djamel_Belayachi-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Within days the riots spread to twenty-odd <i><a href="/wiki/Wilayah" title="Wilayah">wilayahs</a></i>, covering almost the whole of the north including the <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a> region,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> as well as some towns in the <a href="/wiki/Sahara" title="Sahara">Sahara</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Ouargla" title="Ouargla">Ouargla</a><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bechar" class="mw-redirect" title="Bechar">Bechar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Government buildings, particularly town halls, were widely targeted, and shops in some areas were looted or burned;<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> some of the looters carried swords.<sup id="cite_ref-Yasmine_Ryan_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yasmine_Ryan-28">[28]</a></sup> Football matches scheduled for 7 and 8 January were cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-Yasmine_Ryan_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yasmine_Ryan-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 January, the government agreed to a temporary cut in taxes and duties on <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cooking_oil" title="Cooking oil">cooking oil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Beatrice_Khadige_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Beatrice_Khadige-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Censorship_of_Facebook" title="Censorship of Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/Twitter#Censorship" title="Twitter">Twitter</a> access were also restricted in some areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Belmadi_Censure_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Belmadi_Censure-29">[29]</a></sup> The rioting continued, at least up to 10 January in some places, such as the Bachdjarrah neighbourood in Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> By 11 January, the situation had calmed. An attempt to demonstrate on 11 January in Algiers, organised in advance by the intercommunal committee of Ain Benian and Staoueli, was repressed vigorously by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> In total, three demonstrators died, more than 800 people had been wounded, and at least 1,100 were arrested, many of them minors.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_implications">Political implications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Political implications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While riots on this scale are unprecedented since the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_1991" title="Algerian legislative election, 1991">1991 election</a>, their wider political implications are not yet clear. The rioters had no collective ties to any Algerian political party, organisation, or trade union,<sup id="cite_ref-Hugh_Roberts_FP_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hugh_Roberts_FP-33">[33]</a></sup> and some sources commented that they seemed to have no political slogans.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Some opposition groups emphasised the riots' political dimension; ex-diplomat and opposition spokesperson <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Larbi_Zitout" title="Mohamed Larbi Zitout">Mohamed Larbi Zitout</a> described them as "a revolt, and probably a revolution, of an oppressed people",<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Forces_Front" title="Socialist Forces Front">Socialist Forces Front</a> responded to the government's lowering of food prices on 8 January with the slogan "The government cannot buy Algerians' silence".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agence_France-Presse" title="Agence France-Presse">Agence France-Presse</a> (AFP) has linked the January protests with events in Tunisia, stating, "In Tunisia, <a href="/wiki/Tunisian_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Tunisian revolution">similar unrest</a> sparked the overthrow of the government of <a href="/wiki/Zine_El_Abidine_Ben_Ali" title="Zine El Abidine Ben Ali">Zine Al Abidine Ben Ali</a>, whose 23 years in power ended with his flight to <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> last Friday. Algerian commentators have said that more Tunisia-style protests could break out in Algeria."<sup id="cite_ref-jordantimes_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordantimes-38">[38]</a></sup> Despite their scale, the riots were dealt with by the government in much the same way as the localised riots that had already become a routine way of communicating grievances: it sought to avoid creating <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">martyrs</a> and made a specific concession (in this case, a return to the <i>status quo ante</i> of allowing un-declared food sales by <a href="/wiki/Cevital" title="Cevital">Cevital</a>) not seen as threatening the overall system.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Self-immolations_.28starting_12_January.29">Self-immolations (starting 12 January)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Self-immolations (starting 12 January)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2011_Algerian_self-immolations" title="2011 Algerian self-immolations">2011 Algerian self-immolations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mohsen_Bouterfif.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/91/Mohsen_Bouterfif.jpg/170px-Mohsen_Bouterfif.jpg" width="170" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/91/Mohsen_Bouterfif.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="202" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mohsen_Bouterfif.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mohsen Bouterfif in the hospital showing the wounds from his self-immolation</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As the widely reported protests sparked off by <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bouazizi" title="Mohamed Bouazizi">Mohamed Bouazizi</a>'s self-immolation in Tunisia began to have a clear impact on the Tunisian government, a wave of <a href="/wiki/Self-immolation" title="Self-immolation">self-immolations</a> swept Algeria. These individual acts of protest mostly took place in front of a government building following an unsuccessful approach to the authorities. Four self-immolators have died of their burns so far.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>It began on 12 January, when 26-year-old Mohamed Aouichia set himself on fire in <a href="/wiki/Bordj_Menaiel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bordj Menaiel">Bordj Menaiel</a> in the compound of the <i><a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Algeria" title="Districts of Algeria">daira</a></i> building. He had been sharing a room of 30 square metres with seven other people, including his sister, since 2003; he had repeatedly approached local authorities to get on the social housing list and been rebuffed.<sup id="cite_ref-courrierinternational1_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-courrierinternational1-42">[42]</a></sup> He has so far survived.</p>
<p>On 13 January, <a href="/wiki/Mohsen_Bouterfif" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohsen Bouterfif">Mohsen Bouterfif</a>, a 37-year-old father of two, set himself on fire. He had gone with about twenty other youths to protest in front of the town hall of <a href="/wiki/Boukhadra" title="Boukhadra">Boukhadra</a> in Tebessa demanding jobs and houses, after the mayor refused to receive them. According to one testimony, the mayor shouted to them: "If you have courage, do like Bouazizi did, set yourself on fire!"<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> His death was reported on 16 January, and about 100 youths protested his death causing the provincial governor to sack the mayor.<sup id="cite_ref-bouterfif_aljaz_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bouterfif_aljaz-44">[44]</a></sup> However, hospital staff the following day claimed he was still alive, though in critical condition.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> described the suicide as "echoing the <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bouazizi#Confiscation_of_wares_and_self-immolation" title="Mohamed Bouazizi">self-immolation</a> that triggered the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Tunisian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–2011 Tunisian protests">protests</a> that toppled the leader of neighbouring Tunisia."<sup id="cite_ref-bouterfif_aljaz_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bouterfif_aljaz-44">[44]</a></sup> He finally died on 24 January at a hospital in Annaba.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>These suicides were followed by dozens more attempted or successful self-immolations across the country, so far without triggering nationwide demonstrations, most of them after the Tunisian dictator <a href="/wiki/Zine_El_Abidine_Ben_Ali" title="Zine El Abidine Ben Ali">Zine El Abidine Ben Ali</a> fled his country on 14 January.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Response_of_the_parties_and_unions">Response of the parties and unions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Response of the parties and unions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_January_2011">Late January 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Late January 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg/220px-110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg/330px-110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg/440px-110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:110109_Algeria_slashes_food_prices_amid_riots_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Protesters</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A number of left-wing opposition parties, including the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Forces_Front" title="Socialist Forces Front">FFS</a>, RCD, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Party_of_Liberty_and_Justice&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Party of Liberty and Justice (page does not exist)">PLJ</a>, and the Communist <a href="/wiki/Democratic_and_Social_Movement_(Algeria)" title="Democratic and Social Movement (Algeria)">MDS</a>, as well as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Algerian_League_for_Human_Rights&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Algerian League for Human Rights (page does not exist)">Algerian League for Human Rights</a> (LADDH) and officially unrecognised unions, such as SATEF and SNAPAP, met on 20 January to discuss responses to the situation. On 21 January, several of them (excluding the FFS<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>) formed the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Coordination_Nationale_pour_le_Changement_et_la_D%C3%A9mocratie&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coordination Nationale pour le Changement et la Démocratie (page does not exist)">Coordination Nationale pour le Changement et la Démocratie</a> (National Coordination for Change and Democracy), seeking systemic change within the country<sup id="cite_ref-afrik_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrik-4">[4]</a></sup> and calling (along with <a href="/wiki/Rachad" title="Rachad">Rachad</a><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>) for nationwide marches, starting 9 February.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The Interior Minister, <a href="/wiki/Ould_Kablia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ould Kablia">Ould Kablia</a>, responded that "No march would be authorised by the authorities in Algiers... Marches are forbidden in Algiers."<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meanwhile, the mainly <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabyle</a>-based secularist <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Culture_and_Democracy" title="Rally for Culture and Democracy">RCD</a> party had announced plans for a march for democracy to be held on Saturday 22 January, despite being refused permission by the government<sup id="cite_ref-jordantimes_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jordantimes-38">[38]</a></sup> under the state of emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-army_should_quit_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army_should_quit-5">[5]</a></sup> Prior to the March, RCD leader <a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Sadi" title="Saïd Sadi">Saïd Sadi</a> linked the planned march to the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%932011_Tunisian_protests" class="mw-redirect" title="2010–2011 Tunisian protests">2010–2011 Tunisian protests</a>, stating, "If the opposition does not mobilise the crowds, we believe that we will have more devastating events than what happened in Tunisia. The anger here is bigger than (it was) in Tunisia."<sup id="cite_ref-army_should_quit_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army_should_quit-5">[5]</a></sup> He also called for the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_civil_war#Elections_cancelled:_a_guerrilla_war_begins" class="mw-redirect" title="Algerian civil war">1992</a> state of emergency to be lifted and for the army to withdraw from politics, stating, "The army should no longer be a decision maker, it has to become a state institution."<sup id="cite_ref-army_should_quit_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-army_should_quit-5">[5]</a></sup> The march attracted about 300 people, and was broken up by the police; 42 people (according to the RCD<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>) or 19 (according to the Interior Ministry<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>) were injured, and 9, including the head of the party's parliamentary group Othman Amazouz, were arrested, to be released later the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Some demonstrators waved the <a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisian</a> flag, alluding to the protests which had brought down Ben Ali.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Would-be demonstrators coming from <a href="/wiki/Tizi_Ouzou" title="Tizi Ouzou">Tizi Ouzou</a> were prevented from reaching the scene by the police.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> On 22 January, 20,000 police officers stopped all protests. In the ensuing clash five people were killed and more than 800 others hurt.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz_alg_12Feb_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz_alg_12Feb-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 January, the FFS and LADDH jointly issued a demand for the release of the demonstrators arrested in early January, in <a href="/wiki/Tizi-Ouzou" class="mw-redirect" title="Tizi-Ouzou">Tizi-Ouzou</a> and elsewhere;<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> students of <a href="/wiki/Tizi-Ouzou" class="mw-redirect" title="Tizi-Ouzou">Tizi-Ouzou</a> announced plans for a march on 1 February demanding their release and economic development for Kabylie.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 29 January, the RCD organised a march of over ten thousand people (according to the organisers) in the city of <a href="/wiki/Bejaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bejaia">Bejaia</a>, to demand more freedom and democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_February_2011">Early February 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Early February 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Protests continued on 3 February. On the same day President Abdelaziz Bouteflika signaled at a meeting with government ministers his intention to lift the 19-year-old state of emergency in the "very near future", in what was seen as an attempt to quell opposition demands. Reportedly, he also urged the cabinet to adopt measures to promote job creation and said Algeria's TV and radio should give airtime to all political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> On 4 February, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> reported that demonstrations were planned for 12 February.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz_febdominos_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz_febdominos-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>While Bouteflika was said to be working to counter the planned demonstration, on 8 February university students commenced an "indefinite strike" in protest against the "poor quality of teaching."<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> On the same day, an indefinite strike was also launched by professional paramedics after a call by the trade union SAP. However, it was reported to have been observed in only 22 of the country's 48 provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="12_February">12 February</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 12 February">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The day after Egyptian President <a href="/wiki/Hosni_Mubarak" title="Hosni Mubarak">Hosni Mubarak</a> resigned, the protest gained new currency.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazlive_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazlive-66">[66]</a></sup> The protests were organised by the nascent National Co-ordination for Change and Democracy, an umbrella group of opposition parties, civil society groups and unofficial unions.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12feb_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12feb-67">[67]</a></sup> The police blocked all entry points into Algiers<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_alg_12Feb_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_alg_12Feb-68">[68]</a></sup> and put in a security cordon around <a href="/w/index.php?title=May_First_Square&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="May First Square (page does not exist)">May First Square</a> in central Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz_alg_12Feb_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz_alg_12Feb-2">[2]</a></sup> All opposition rallies were banned by the government, though at least 2,000 protesters forced their way through the security cordon around the Square to join other demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12feb_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12feb-67">[67]</a></sup> Though minor protests occurred earlier in the day, most protesters came out after noon;<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12febblog_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12febblog-69">[69]</a></sup> several thousand protestors<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_alg_12Feb_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_alg_12Feb-68">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> clashed with about 30,000 police at May First Square in central Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz_alg_12Feb_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz_alg_12Feb-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt_alg_12Feb_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_alg_12Feb-68">[68]</a></sup> Protesters chanted "<i>Djazair Horra Dimocratia</i>," ("A free and democratic Algeria") "<i>système dégage</i>" ("government out") and "Yesterday Egypt, today Algeria."<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Police fired tear gas<sup id="cite_ref-aljazlive_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazlive-66">[66]</a></sup> on the protesters and arrested hundreds<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz_alg_12Feb_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz_alg_12Feb-2">[2]</a></sup> to possibly more than a 10,000 people,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Algeria" title="Human rights in Algeria">human rights</a> activists and <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade union</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> The Algerian League for the Defense of Human Rights said that up to 28,000 police officers were deployed in Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12feb_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12feb-67">[67]</a></sup> Many people, including a member of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_National_Assembly" title="People's National Assembly">People's National Assembly</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Boubkeur_Derguini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boubkeur Derguini (page does not exist)">Boubkeur Derguini</a><sup id="cite_ref-assemblee_Boubkeur_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-assemblee_Boubkeur-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Derguini_name_note_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Derguini_name_note-75">[75]</a></sup> of the RCD, were injured.<sup id="cite_ref-algsoir_feb12_arrests_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-algsoir_feb12_arrests-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Protesters had hoped to stay the night at the main square.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> At almost 19:30, <i><a href="/wiki/Thomson_Reuters" title="Thomson Reuters">Thomson Reuters</a></i> reported hundreds of people were leaving the demonstrations after about three hours and that the police opened their cordon to let them pass. It also said that about 200 young men from a poor neighbourhood stayed on and that some of them threw objects at the police.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12febblog_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12febblog-69">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ThomsReut_Feb12_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThomsReut_Feb12-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<p>Protests were also reported in <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Algeria" title="Constantine, Algeria">Constantine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">Oran</a>. There were reports of internet services like Twitter, Facebook and the wider internet to have been disrupted or shut down,<sup id="cite_ref-aljazlive_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazlive-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> however, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Renesys&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Renesys (page does not exist)">Renesys</a></i> denied this had taken place.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sa%C3%AFd_Sadi" title="Saïd Sadi">Saïd Sadi</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Culture_and_Democracy" title="Rally for Culture and Democracy">RCD</a> interpreted the large number of police as government weakness, stating, "When you mobilize 30,000 police in the capital, that's a sign of weakness, not strength."<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_alg_12Feb_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt_alg_12Feb-68">[68]</a></sup> He also said that police charged at protesters and arrested 10 people outside the party offices as they celebrated Mubarak's resignation.<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12feb_67-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12feb-67">[67]</a></sup> He added that 90-year-old human rights activist Ali Yahia Abdelnour was "manhandled by the police" and that the protesters were not "an organised demonstration. It was spontaneous. It was an explosion of joy."<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12febblog_69-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12febblog-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="13.E2.80.9318_February">13–18 February</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 13–18 February">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 13 February, following a suggestion by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ali_Yahia_Abdennour&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ali Yahia Abdennour (page does not exist)">Ali Yahia Abdennour</a> of the LADDH,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> the CNCD<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> called for protests to continue every Saturday in the same square in Algiers, a call confirmed by RCD spokesman Mohsen Belabbes; Ali Yahia Abdennour said that "we will gather momentum as we progress we want our dignity back, yesterday the police has brutally beaten many protesters amongst them a pregnant women, old ladies, a journalist, young men and women, we should carry on protesting until we get our rights." The next day the activist blogger Hchicha called for alternative marches on Friday as well, meant to attract people wanting a change of system but distrusting the political parties involved in the CNCD.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Elias Filali reported that police had used tear gas to disperse protesters and to evict families who had occupied newly constructed homes overnight in Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-aljazblog13feb_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazblog13feb-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 February, Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Mourad_Medelci" title="Mourad Medelci">Mourad Medelci</a> said the state of emergency would be lifted "within days."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Two days later, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Ouyahia" title="Ahmed Ouyahia">Ahmed Ouyahia</a> announced the state of emergency would be lifted by the end of February.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>Former FLN leader <a href="/wiki/Abdelhamid_Mehri" title="Abdelhamid Mehri">Abdelhamid Mehri</a> called for true democracy, saying the current regime was incapable of solving the country's problems.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 February, a date for which a <i>Facebook</i> group had called for protests, police with water cannons were deployed in the main crossroads of Algiers.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_February">Late February</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Late February">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Thousands turned out in Algiers for protests but were unable to take control of the main square.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<p>The government officially announces the end of the emergency rule. The country’s council of ministers adopted a law revoking the 1993 decree that prolonged a state of emergency originally instituted the previous year, stating that the “law will come into effect as soon as its imminent publication in the official journal”.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>The state of emergency in the country was officially lifted after being published in the country's <a href="/wiki/Official_journal" class="mw-redirect" title="Official journal">official journal</a>, responding to one of the main demands of the protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-wp_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-92">[92]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> The move legalizes protests outside the capital of Algiers, as long as the government is notified of planned demonstrations at least three days in advance.<sup id="cite_ref-wp_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-92">[92]</a></sup> According to the country's interior minister, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dahou_Ould_Kabila&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dahou Ould Kabila (page does not exist)">Dahou Ould Kabila</a>, protests are still banned within Algiers because of security concerns; he said that "Algiers is targeted by leaders of terrorist groups [because] it gives them media impact.<sup id="cite_ref-wp_92-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-92">[92]</a></sup> The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Algerian_League_for_the_Defense_of_Human_Rights&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Algerian League for the Defense of Human Rights (page does not exist)">Algerian League for the Defense of Human Rights</a>, a leader of the protests, said it was a "ruse aimed at fooling international opinion at a time when Arab regimes are under pressure."<sup id="cite_ref-wp_92-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wp-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="March">March</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: March">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Protests continue throughout Algiers, although it is reported that the government has been keeping the country stable, although this momentary peace is expected to end soon.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 March, protests organised by the <a href="/w/index.php?title=National_Co-ordination_for_Democracy_and_Change&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="National Co-ordination for Democracy and Change (page does not exist)">National Co-ordination for Democracy and Change</a> in Algiers were violently suppressed while in al-Madania neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">Algiers</a>, a group of youths, wearing banners supporting Abdelaziz Bouteflika, tried to lynch opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Said_Sadi" class="mw-redirect" title="Said Sadi">Said Sadi</a>, the president of the <a href="/wiki/Rally_for_Culture_and_Democracy" title="Rally for Culture and Democracy">Rally for Culture and Democracy</a>. Meanwhile, Algeria's oldest opposition party, <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Forces_Front" title="Socialist Forces Front">Socialist Forces Front</a>, has urged Algerians to engage in a "peaceful struggle" for change in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 March, thousands of community police rallied in the capital Algiers despite a protest ban in the city, accusing the government of ingratitude, and insisting thousands of their colleagues have been killed or injured fighting Islamist violence. Demanding better pay and pensions, they got all the way to the Parliament building.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Algiers, small group of around 150 or so threw <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktails" class="mw-redirect" title="Molotov cocktails">Molotov cocktails</a> at much larger crowd of police.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 March, police in the Algiers suburb of Oued Koriche used tear gas on Wednesday to disperse a crowd of young men who threw stones and <a href="/wiki/Molotov_Cocktails" class="mw-redirect" title="Molotov Cocktails">Molotov Cocktails</a> trying to stop bulldozers from demolishing dozens of illegally built homes. Five police officers were injured in the rioting, during which rioters threw bricks down on police from nearby rooftop and set fire to a car.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April.E2.80.93May">April–May</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: April–May">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 15 April, in a long-awaited televised address, President Abdelaziz Bouteflika said he would seek constitutional amendments that would "reinforce representative democracy" and be submitted to parliament or to a referendum. He also proposed changes to laws on elections, the media or political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 May, 1,500 Doctors attempted to march towards government buildings but were prevented by anti-riot police.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February_2012">February 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: February 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In late February 2012, Algeria's major <a href="/wiki/Islamism" title="Islamism">Islamist</a> parties announced a coalition ahead of <a href="/wiki/Algerian_legislative_election,_2012" title="Algerian legislative election, 2012">parliamentary elections</a>. A leader of the <a href="/wiki/Movement_of_Society_for_Peace" title="Movement of Society for Peace">Movement of Society for Peace</a> called for more opposition parties to join the alliance "to give the best possible chance for the Arab Spring to happen in Algeria as well".<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_protests_over_jobs_and_infrastructure">Local protests over jobs and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Local protests over jobs and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Late_January_2011_2">Late January 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Late January 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marchedignite.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marchedignite.jpg/200px-Marchedignite.jpg" width="200" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marchedignite.jpg/300px-Marchedignite.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Marchedignite.jpg/400px-Marchedignite.jpg 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="563" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marchedignite.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Students marching to <a href="/wiki/El-Mouradia" class="mw-redirect" title="El-Mouradia">el-Mouradia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The opposition group <a href="/wiki/Rachad" title="Rachad">Rachad</a> uploaded film of a non-violent demonstration of "more than 1000 people" demanding housing in the Said Hamdine neighbourhood of Algiers on 20 January, not widely reported.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 January, more than 500 people demonstrated in front of the <i>daira</i> building of <a href="/wiki/Khemis_El_Khechna" class="mw-redirect" title="Khemis El Khechna">Khemis El Khechna</a>, demanding water and gas connection and better housing for their nearby hometowns, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chebacheb&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Chebacheb (page does not exist)">Chebacheb</a> and <a href="/wiki/El_Kerma" title="El Kerma">El Kerma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Tizi_Ouzou" title="Tizi Ouzou">Tizi Ouzou</a> the same day, parents of youths detained in the protests of early January staged a sit-in in front of the <a href="/wiki/Wilaya" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilaya">wilaya</a> seat building, demanding the release of their children,<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> who were provisionally released the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 January, the inhabitants of El Djezzar in <a href="/wiki/Batna_Province" title="Batna Province">Batna</a> occupied their <a href="/wiki/Town_hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Town hall">town hall</a>, demanding a better <a href="/wiki/Road" title="Road">road</a> to their village.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> On the same day, about a hundred inhabitants of Boutaleb near <a href="/wiki/Chekfa" title="Chekfa">Chekfa</a> blocked the main road, demanding gas and sewage connection for their town and better side roads.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 27 January, hundreds of inhabitants of Choukrane near <a href="/wiki/Bouira" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouira">Bouira</a> closed the nearby national road (RN 29), demanding gas, water, a sewage system, and public lighting, as well as speed bumps to reduce traffic fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> On the same day, dozens of unemployed youths blocked RN 12 in <a href="/wiki/Naciria" title="Naciria">Naciria</a> near <a href="/wiki/Boumerdes" class="mw-redirect" title="Boumerdes">Boumerdes</a> using burning tyres and other objects, demanding jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 30 January, unemployed youths closed the APC seat of <a href="/wiki/Belaas" class="mw-redirect" title="Belaas">Belaas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ain_Defla" class="mw-redirect" title="Ain Defla">Ain Defla</a>, demanding jobs (according to the mayor), as well as better water and road management.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> On the same day, 600 factory workers demonstrated in front of the wilaya seat in <a href="/wiki/Bouira" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouira">Bouira</a>, demanding to be re-hired by ENAD.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Also on the same day, unemployed youths in the wilaya of <a href="/wiki/Ouargla_Province" title="Ouargla Province">Ouargla</a> demonstrated in <a href="/wiki/Touggourt" title="Touggourt">Touggourt</a> against the head of the local employment bureau, accused of favouritism.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February_2011">February 2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: February 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 February, the people of Raffour in <a href="/w/index.php?title=M%27chedallah&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="M'chedallah (page does not exist)">M'chedallah</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bouira" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouira">Bouira</a> blocked national route 26 with burning tyres, demanding public lighting, a sewage system, and town planning. <sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> On the same day, the population of Tazgait in <a href="/wiki/Mostaghanem" class="mw-redirect" title="Mostaghanem">Mostaghanem</a> closed their town hall, demanding that the mayor leave office for failing to do enough about the region's underdevelopment. <sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 7 February, youths at Toumiate in <a href="/wiki/El_Harrouch" title="El Harrouch">El Harrouch</a> near <a href="/wiki/Skikda" title="Skikda">Skikda</a> blocked the national highway RN 3, and were attacked by riot police using tear gas.<sup id="cite_ref-Alg.C3.A9rie_Focus_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alg.C3.A9rie_Focus-115">[115]</a></sup> On 8 February, youths in <a href="/wiki/Sidi_Amar,_Annaba" title="Sidi Amar, Annaba">Sidi Amar</a> near <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> demonstrated to demand jobs, blocking the road and burning tyres.<sup id="cite_ref-Alg.C3.A9rie_Focus_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alg.C3.A9rie_Focus-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>From 6 to 9 February, protesters closed the national highway RN 26 at <a href="/wiki/El_Kseur" class="mw-redirect" title="El Kseur">El Kseur</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bejaia" class="mw-redirect" title="Bejaia">Bejaia</a>, demanding their jobs back or better compensation after the EPBTP milk factory where they were employed made them redundant. <sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 and 9 February, youths in <a href="/wiki/Naciria" title="Naciria">Naciria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bordj-Menaiel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bordj-Menaiel">Bordj-Menaiel</a> attacked ANEM offices, confronted police, and closed the national highway RN 12, protesting unemployment and unfulfilled government promises of jobs. <sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 February, a crowd of youths gathered in front of the <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> wilaya office demanding the 7000 jobs they had previously been promised, and greeted the governor with stone-throwing when he came out. One attempted to commit suicide, but was dissuaded by his brother.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 14 February, hundreds of youths protested over unemployment in <a href="/wiki/Akbou" title="Akbou">Akbou</a>; about 30 were hurt in clashes with the police.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 February, youths in <a href="/wiki/Tadmait" class="mw-redirect" title="Tadmait">Tadmait</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tizi-Ouzou" class="mw-redirect" title="Tizi-Ouzou">Tizi-Ouzou</a>) went out on the streets demanding jobs, blocking the roads (including RN 12) with burning tires and damaging the APC office. Five of them were arrested after confrontations with anti-riot police.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Also on 16 February, about 80 unemployed youths occupied the daira offices in <a href="/wiki/Hassi-Messaoud" class="mw-redirect" title="Hassi-Messaoud">Hassi-Messaoud</a> in protest against poverty and "hogra" (oppression) in the region that provides most of the country's oil income,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> and were dislodged by promises of jobs next week after hundreds of police and gendarmes gathered. On 17 February, about 500 youths demonstrated in front of the same daira office.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Another 100 unemployed youths demonstrated in nearby <a href="/wiki/Touggourt" title="Touggourt">Touggourt</a>, in front of the local office of the National Employment Agency.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 17 February, the <a href="/wiki/Annaba" title="Annaba">Annaba</a> wilaya offices were again targeted by demonstrators demanding jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 21 February, hundreds of students protesting in front of the Ministry of Higher Education against the new LMD system were dispersed forcibly by police.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Ammal" title="Ammal">Ammal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Boumerdes" class="mw-redirect" title="Boumerdes">Boumerdes</a>), demonstrators closed the local APC offices, demanding better housing.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 23 February, villagers from nearby Imaghzarene closed the daira offices of <a href="/wiki/Draa_El_Mizan" class="mw-redirect" title="Draa El Mizan">Draa El Mizan</a>, demanding paving, public lighting, gas, more housing, and a clinic for their town.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> At <a href="/wiki/Ammi_Moussa" title="Ammi Moussa">Ammi Moussa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Relizane" title="Relizane">Relizane</a>) dozens of youths gathered to blockade the town hall, demanding that the president and secretary-general of the APC resign. <sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> On the same day, doctors in the <a href="/wiki/Sidi_Bel_Abbes" class="mw-redirect" title="Sidi Bel Abbes">Sidi Bel Abbes</a> maternity ward staged a sit-in in protest against the lack of pharmaceutical supplies, which they said was preventing them from carrying out operations.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bouzareah" class="mw-redirect" title="Bouzareah">Bouzareah</a> university students announced a strike demanding greater security at the university after a woman student was attacked by unknown assailants, who slashed her face, on campus grounds.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 February, unemployed youths gathered in front of the mayoralty of <a href="/wiki/Sidi_Lakhdar" title="Sidi Lakhdar">Sidi Lakhdar</a> near <a href="/wiki/Mostaganem" title="Mostaganem">Mostaganem</a>, after blocking the road (RN11) the previous day; they left when the mayor promised to review the housing lists.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Djelida" title="Djelida">Djelida</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ain_Defla" class="mw-redirect" title="Ain Defla">Ain Defla</a>), the same day, about 500 people closed the APC offices, demanding jobs and protesting at the allocation of 117 new jobs to people from outside the region.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="January_2012">January 2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: January 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 10 January, Algerians protested in <a href="/wiki/Laghouat" title="Laghouat">Laghouat</a> over housing, infrastructure, and treatment of the elderly by police. The police used tear gas to disperse the protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ramadan_2013">Ramadan 2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Ramadan 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After security forces question three youths who were eating lunch in the <a href="/wiki/Kabylie" title="Kabylie">Kabylie</a> region during <a href="/wiki/Ramadan" title="Ramadan">Ramadan</a>, about 300 others joined a protest lunch against the mandatory nature of fasting during the month. The head of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kabylie_Autonomy_Movement&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kabylie Autonomy Movement (page does not exist)">Kabylie Autonomy Movement</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bouaziz_Ait_Chebib&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bouaziz Ait Chebib (page does not exist)">Bouaziz Ait Chebib</a> said: "We called this gathering to denounce the inquisition and persecution of citizens who, because of their beliefs, refuse to observe the fast."<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reactions">Reactions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010%E2%80%9312_Algerian_protests&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Reactions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dt>Domestic</dt>
</dl>
<p>In reaction to the protests of early January, starting 8 January the government decreased the prices of essential foods. Over following weeks it increased wheat supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 February Bouteflika announced plans to lift the emergency law, which prohibits protests without a permit, and substitute for it new anti-terrorism laws,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> but said that protests would remain illegal in Algiers in any case "for well-known reasons of public order".<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> He also announced new measures to create jobs and that state-run television and radio should be open to all political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> On 14 February, his foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Mourad_Medelci" title="Mourad Medelci">Mourad Medelci</a> repeated the promise to end the state of emergency law, saying it would happen by the end of the month.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> on 22 February the cabinet voted to lift the emergency law. It also voted on a measure to alleviate unemployment.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>In efforts to discourage the protests organised by the CNCD, the authorities played up the role of the RCD, a mainly Kabyle party unpopular elsewhere in the country, within them; while this tactic had some success, it did not stop demonstrators from turning out in some non-Kabyle cities.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>International</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/23px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/35px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/45px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="540" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> – <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_European_Parliament" title="President of the European Parliament">President</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> <a href="/wiki/Jerzy_Buzek" title="Jerzy Buzek">Jerzy Buzek</a> said that he "call[ed] upon the Algerian authorities to refrain from violence and respect their citizens' right to peaceful demonstration. Any and all demonstrators arrested should be released immediately. The continuing state of emergency is unjustifiable and clearly hampers Algeria's prospects for the fair, peaceful and sustainable development of the country. It is but a first step in responding to the legitimate democratic aspirations of the Algerian people, but even this step has yet to materialise. Opposition groups, civil society, and especially young people should have the right to freely express their criticism of the government. No government can ignore the call of its people."</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> – Foreign Ministry spokesman Bernard Valero said regarding the demonstrations that "What is important in our eyes us is that freedom of expression is respected and that the demonstrations are able to take place freely and without violence", and welcomed the planned end to the State of Emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> – Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Guido_Westerwelle" title="Guido Westerwelle">Guido Westerwelle</a> said Germany was "on the side of democrats. The German government calls on the Algerian government to renounce all recourse to violence. These are demonstrators who want freedom, who are doing nothing more than exercising a human right, to know the right to defend with dignity their point of view. As democrats we are on the side of democrats. I have already said that about Tunisia and Egypt. I say it again now in allusion to other countries."<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> – <a href="/wiki/Department_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of State">Department of State</a> spokesman PJ Crowley said that "We note the ongoing protests in Algeria, and call for restraint on the part of the security services. In addition, we reaffirm our support for the universal rights of the Algerian people, including assembly and expression. These rights apply on the internet. Moreover, these rights must be respected. We will continue to follow the situation closely in the days ahead."<sup id="cite_ref-aljazblog13feb_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazblog13feb-84">[84]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Other</dt>
</dl>
<p>Regional financial stock market indices fell on 20 February on concern of spreading instability.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dt>NGOs</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda_in_the_Islamic_Maghreb" title="Al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb">al-Qaeda in the Islamic Maghreb</a> voiced support for the demonstrators against both the Tunisian and Algerian governments in a video released on 13 January 2011. AQIM leader <a href="/wiki/Abu_Musab_Abdul_Wadud" class="mw-redirect" title="Abu Musab Abdul Wadud">Abu Musab Abdul Wadud</a> offered military aid and training to the demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> issued a statement that read: "Algerians must be allowed to express themselves freely and hold peaceful protests in Algiers and elsewhere. We urge the Algerian authorities not to respond to these demands by using excessive force."<sup id="cite_ref-aljaz12feb_67-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljaz12feb-67">[67]</a></sup></li>
<li>On 21 January, the international group <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(group)" title="Anonymous (group)">Anonymous</a> declared a cyber-war on the Algerian state on the grounds of censorship, following previous efforts in Tunisia.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> The next day they brought down the pro-government <a href="/wiki/National_Rally_for_Democracy_(Algeria)" title="National Rally for Democracy (Algeria)">RND</a> party website, having previously brought down the sites of the Ministry of the Interior and the <a href="/wiki/Entreprise_nationale_de_t%C3%A9l%C3%A9vision" class="mw-redirect" title="Entreprise nationale de télévision">national TV station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
